## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching a second-order oscillator written as a first-order system. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators typically express dv_dt as combinations of restoring forces in x, damping forces in v, and possible explicit time-dependent (driven/parametric) forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Free particle / constant acceleration: dv_dt = c0 (baseline or constant external force)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude restoring acceleration; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear damping + linear restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (viscous damping with linear spring)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order potential nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag-like): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipation)
- Rayleigh damping (odd polynomial in v): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (self-excited/velocity-dependent dissipation)
- van der Pol form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit-cycle formation)
- Pendulum (sinusoidal restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle oscillator)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic drive)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type dynamics)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping + drive): dv_dt = -1 * (c0 * x + c1 * x**3) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (common decomposition into restoring, nonlinear restoring, damping, forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force from a potential: polynomial-in-x terms (x, x**3, x**5) typically indicate expansion of a nonlinear spring potential around equilibrium.
- Pendulum-like geometry: sin(c*x) restoring suggests bounded periodic potential and amplitude-dependent frequency (nonlinear period).
- Dissipation strength vs speed: terms like v, v*Abs(v), v**3 encode increasingly strong damping at higher velocities and change ring-down rates.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: a factor (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v indicates negative damping in one regime and positive damping in another, producing stable oscillations.
- External periodic drive: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms imply resonance peaks and steady-state forced oscillations with phase lag.
- Parametric resonance: time-multiplying-x factors like (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x indicate stiffness modulation leading to instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Autonomous vs non-autonomous identification: absence of explicit t often indicates a conservative/damped autonomous oscillator; explicit t usually implies driving or parametric modulation.
- Odd/even symmetry cues: only odd powers of x (x, x**3, ...) often reflect symmetric potentials about x=0; inclusion of even powers can indicate asymmetry or bias.

Structure desc      : Additive mix of (near-zero) linear x, modest linear v, two time-only exponential terms, and a sharply varying odd-in-x rational term x/(c9+|x|)^3. The x-linear coefficient is tiny (c0≈-0.00286), so x influence is dominated by the last term with large magnitude (c8≈-23.9), which behaves roughly like a scaled linear x near 0 and decays as 1/|x|^2 for large |x|. The time oscillatory exp(c5 sin) is mild here (c5≈-0.176 gives only ~±20% modulation), so the formula is approximately 0.0646v + 0.685 e^{-0.278 t} −0.593·exp(−0.176 sin(1.011 t+6.067)) −23.9·x/(2.67+|x|)^3.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO23)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
0.10853689295113\sin(t)\;-\;0.445567501246416\log(|v|+1)\;-\;1.1449635767559\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **all three** of these structural pieces simultaneously:

1) a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no \(x,v\) dependence),  
2) a \(\log(|v|+1)\) term (log of absolute velocity plus 1),  
3) an \(x e^{-|x|}\) term (linear in \(x\) times an exponential in \(|x|\), not a rational function of \(|x|\), not \(\tanh\), etc.).

Also, the \(|v|\) inside the log is essential (cannot be replaced by \(v\) or \(|v|^{1/3}\), etc.), and \(\exp(-|x|)\) is essential (cannot be replaced by \(1/(c+|x|)^k\) or \(x/(c+|x|^3)\), etc.).

Now check each candidate for whether it even has the right *functional forms* available (constants can be set to 0 to remove extra terms).

---

### 1
Has linear \(x\), linear \(v\), exponentials in \(t\), exp(sin(...)), and \(x/(c+|x|)^3\).  
No \(\log(|v|+1)\). No \(x e^{-|x|}\). No plain \(\sin(t)\) (only inside exp(sin)).  
**No match.**

### 2
Has rational-in-\(x\), \(x/(c+|x|^3)\), constant, \(|v|^{1/3}\), and \(\sin(\cdot)\).  
No \(\log(|v|+1)\). No \(x e^{-|x|}\).  
**No match.**

### 3
Similar to 2 plus linear \(v\). Still no \(\log(|v|+1)\), no \(x e^{-|x|}\).  
**No match.**

### 4
Has exp(sin(...)) but no \(\log(|v|+1)\), no \(x e^{-|x|}\).  
**No match.**

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO23)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` — a product of x and exp(-|x|)
2. `log(Abs(v) + 1)` — logarithm of |v|+1 (and since v ≤ 0, this is log(-v+1))
3. `sin(t)` — sine of t

Let me analyze each candidate:

### Candidate 1:
`c0*x + c1*v + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*sin(c6*t + c7)) + c8*x/(c9 + Abs(x))**3`

Basis functions: x, v, exp(c3*t), exp(c5*sin(...)), x/(c9+|x|)^3. None of these can produce x*exp(-|x|) or log(|v|+1). The v term is linear, not logarithmic. No match.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2:
`c0*x/(c1 + x) + c2*x/(c3 + Abs(x)**3) + c4 + c5*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)`

Has sin(t) ✓, but uses |v|^(1/3) instead of log(|v|+1), and x/(c1+x) + x/(c3+|x|^3) instead of x*exp(-|x|). These are fundamentally different functions. No match.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3:
`c0*x/(c1 + x) + c2*v + c3*x/(c4 + Abs(x)**3) + c5 + c6*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)`

Similar issues: rational functions of x, v (linear), |v|^(1/3). Cannot match x*exp(-|x|) or log(|v|+1).

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 4:
`c0*x/(c1 + x) + c2*x/(c3 + Abs(x)**3) + c4 + c5*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*t + c9))`

exp(c7*sin(...)) ≠ sin(t). Rational x functions ≠ x*exp(-|x|). |v|^(1/3) ≠ log(|v|+1).

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5:
`c0*x/(c1 + x) + c2*Abs(x)**(1/3) + c3 + c4*v + c5*x/(c6 + Abs(x)**3) + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)`

cos can match sin with phase shift ✓, but v (linear) ≠ log(|v|+1), and rational/power functions of x ≠ x*exp(-|x|).

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6:
`c0*x + c1*v + c2*log(c3*Abs(x) + 1)*cos(c4*t) + c5*x/(c6 + Abs(x))**3 + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)`

Has log(|x|+1)*cos(t) — this couples x and t, which GT doesn't have. Also v (linear) ≠ log(|v|+1). x*exp(-|x|) is not matched by x + x/(c6+|x|)^3.

### Candidate 7:
